type="application/ld+json">{"@context":"https://schema.org","@type":"FAQPage","mainEntity":[{"@type":"Question","name":"What is a Z critical value?","acceptedAnswer":{"@type":"Answer","text":"<div class=\"textBlock\"><p>A Z critical value is the value that defines the <strong>critical region in hypothesis testing</strong> when the test statistic follows the <strong>standard normal distribution</strong>. If the value of the test statistic falls into the critical region, you should reject the null hypothesis and accept the alternative hypothesis.</p></div>"}},{"@type":"Question","name":"How do I calculate Z critical value?","acceptedAnswer":{"@type":"Answer","text":"<div class=\"textBlock\"><p>To find a Z critical value for a given confidence level <code>α</code>:</p>\n<ol>\n<li>Check if you perform a <strong>one- or two-tailed test</strong>.</li>\n<li>For a one-tailed test:\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Left</strong>-tailed: critical value is the <strong><code>α</code>-th</strong> quantile of the standard normal distribution N(0,1).</li>\n<li><strong>Right</strong>-tailed: critical value is the <strong><code>(1-α)</code>-th</strong> quantile.</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li>Two-tailed test: critical value equals <strong><code>±(1-α/2)</code>-th</strong> quantile of N(0,1).</li>\n<li>No <strong>quantile tables</strong>? Use CDF tables! (The quantile function is the inverse of the CDF.)</li>\n<li>Verify your answer with an online critical value calculator.</li>\n</ol></div>"}},{"@type":"Question","name":"Is a t critical value the same as Z critical value?","acceptedAnswer":{"@type":"Answer","text":"<div class=\"textBlock\"><p>In theory, <strong>no</strong>. In practice, very often, <strong>yes</strong>. The t-Student distribution is <strong>similar</strong> to the standard normal distribution, but it is <strong>not the same</strong>. However, if the number of <strong>degrees of freedom</strong> (which is, roughly speaking, the size of your sample) is large enough (&gt;30), then the two distributions are <strong>practically indistinguishable</strong>, and so the t critical value has practically the same value as the Z critical value.</p></div>"}},{"@type":"Question","name":"What is the Z critical value for 95% confidence?","acceptedAnswer":{"@type":"Answer","text":"<div class=\"textBlock\"><p>The Z critical value for a 95% confidence interval is:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>1.96</strong> for a two-tailed test;</li>\n<li><strong>1.64</strong> for a right-tailed test; and</li>\n<li><strong>-1.64</strong> for a left-tailed test.</li>\n</ul></div>"}},{"@type":"Question","name":"What is the significance level, and how is it used in hypothesis testing?","acceptedAnswer":{"@type":"Answer","text":"<div class=\"textBlock\"><p>The significance level is a pre-determined threshold used to decide whether to reject the null hypothesis in a statistical test. The most commonly used significance level is 0.05, which means there is a 5% probability of rejecting the null hypothesis when it is actually true.</p></div>"}},{"@type":"Question","name":"What are the Null hypothesis and alternate hypothesis?","acceptedAnswer":{"@type":"Answer","text":"<div class=\"textBlock\"><p>The null hypothesis (H₀) states that there is no significant difference between the two parameters, such as growth, weight, or any other measured effect. In contrast, the alternative hypothesis (H₁) suggests that there is a significant difference between the two parameters.</p></div>"}}]}</script><link rel="stylesheet" class="e1yds0yu0 css-12nedol e1m4c3o81"><div class="textBlock"><p>Welcome to the critical value calculator! Here you can quickly determine the critical value(s) for <strong>two-tailed</strong> tests, as well as for <strong>one-tailed</strong> tests. It works for most common distributions in statistical testing: the standard normal distribution <strong>N(0,1)</strong> (that is when you have a Z-score), <strong>t-Student, chi-square, and F-distribution</strong>.</p>
<p>What is a critical value? And what is the critical value formula? Scroll down – we provide you with the critical value definition and explain how to calculate critical values in order to use them to construct rejection regions (also known as critical regions).</p></div></div></div></section><style data-emotion="css 1yq5tqa">.css-1yq5tqa{padding:24px 8px 16px;height:266px;display:-webkit-box;display:-webkit-flex;display:-ms-flexbox;display:flex;-webkit-box-pack:center;-ms-flex-pack:center;-webkit-justify-content:center;justify-content:center;box-sizing:content-box;margin-inline:-24px;}</style><section data-testid="article-section-ads" class="css-1yq5tqa euhk33y1"></section><section data-testid="articleSection-0" data-cwv-id="calculator-article-section" id="how-to-use-critical-value-calculator" class="css-qtz96j e1p70fvu0"><style data-emotion="css 1xbj7gb">.css-1xbj7gb{padding:0px;margin:24px 0px 16px;color:#212427;text-align:left;font-family:var(--calculator-ui-font-family);font-size:22px;font-style:normal;font-weight:700;line-height:32px;}</style><h2 data-testid="articleSectionHeader-0" class="css-1xbj7gb">How to use critical value calculator</h2><div data-testid="articleSectionText" class="css-h9evcv e1p70fvu1"><div class="e1yds0yu0 css-12nedol e1m4c3o81"><div class="textBlock"><p>The critical value calculator is your go-to tool for swiftly determining critical values in statistical tests, be it one-tailed or two-tailed. To effectively use the calculator, follow these steps:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>In the first field, input the <strong>distribution of your test statistic</strong> under the null hypothesis: is it a standard normal N (0,1), t-Student, chi-squared, or Snedecor's F? If you are not sure, check the sections below devoted to those distributions, and try to localize the test you need to perform.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In the field <code>What type of test?</code> choose the <strong>alternative hypothesis</strong>: two-tailed, right-tailed, or left-tailed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If needed, specify the <strong>degrees of freedom</strong> of the test statistic's distribution. If you need more clarification, check the description of the test you are performing. You can learn more about the meaning of this quantity in statistics from the <a href="/statistics/degrees-of-freedom" class="js-link">degrees of freedom calculator</a>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Set the significance level,</strong> <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>α</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.43056em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span></span></span></span></span>. By default, we pre-set it to the most common value, 0.05, but you can adjust it to your needs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The critical value calculator will display your critical value(s) and the rejection region(s).</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>For example,</strong> let's envision a scenario where you are conducting a one-tailed hypothesis test using a t-Student distribution with 15 degrees of freedom. You have opted for a right-tailed test and set a significance level (α) of 0.05. The results indicate that the <strong>critical value is 1.7531,</strong> and the critical region is (1.7531, ∞). This implies that if your test statistic exceeds 1.7531, you will reject the null hypothesis at the 0.05 significance level.</p>
<p>👩‍🏫 Want to learn more about critical values? Keep reading!</p></div></div></div></section><section data-testid="articleSection-1" data-cwv-id="calculator-article-section" id="what-is-a-critical-value" class="css-qtz96j e1p70fvu0"><h2 data-testid="articleSectionHeader-1" class="css-1xbj7gb">What is a critical value?</h2><div data-testid="articleSectionText" class="css-h9evcv e1p70fvu1"><div class="e1yds0yu0 css-12nedol e1m4c3o81"><div class="textBlock"><p>In hypothesis testing, critical values are one of the two approaches which allow you to decide whether to retain or reject the null hypothesis. The other approach is to calculate the p-value (for example, using the <a href="/statistics/p-value" class="js-link">p-value calculator</a>).</p>
<p>The critical value approach consists of checking if the value of the test statistic generated by your sample belongs to the so-called <em>rejection region</em>, or <em>critical region</em>, which is the <strong>region where the test statistic is highly improbable to lie</strong>. A critical value is a cut-off value (or two cut-off values in the case of a two-tailed test) that constitutes the boundary of the rejection region(s). In other words, critical values divide the scale of your test statistic into the rejection region and the non-rejection region.</p>
<p>Once you have found the rejection region, <strong>check if the value of the test statistic generated by your sample belongs to it</strong>:</p>
<ul>
<li>If so, it means that you can reject the null hypothesis and accept the alternative hypothesis; and</li>
<li>If not, then there is not enough evidence to reject H<sub>0</sub>.</li>
</ul>
<p>But how to calculate critical values? First of all, you need to <strong>set a significance level</strong>, <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>α</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.43056em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span></span></span></span></span>, which quantifies the probability of rejecting the null hypothesis when it is actually correct. The choice of α is arbitrary; in practice, we most often use a value of 0.05 or 0.01. <strong>Critical values also depend on the alternative hypothesis you choose for your test</strong>, elucidated in the <a href="#critical-value-definition">next section</a>.</p></div></div></div></section><section data-testid="articleSection-2" data-cwv-id="calculator-article-section" id="critical-value-definition" class="css-qtz96j e1p70fvu0"><h2 data-testid="articleSectionHeader-2" class="css-1xbj7gb">Critical value definition</h2><div data-testid="articleSectionText" class="css-h9evcv e1p70fvu1"><div class="e1yds0yu0 css-12nedol e1m4c3o81"><div class="textBlock"><p>To determine critical values, you need to know the distribution of your test statistic under the assumption that the null hypothesis holds. <strong>Critical values are then points with the property that the <strong>probability</strong> of your test statistic assuming values at least as extreme at those critical values is equal to the significance level α</strong>. Wow, quite a definition, isn't it? Don't worry, we'll explain what it all means.</p>
<p>First, let us point out it is the alternative hypothesis that determines what "extreme" means. In particular, if the test is one-sided, then there will be just one critical value; if it is two-sided, then there will be two of them: one to the left and the other to the right of the median value of the distribution.</p>
<p>Critical values can be conveniently depicted as the <strong>points with the property that the area under the density curve of the test statistic from those points to the tails is equal to</strong> <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>α</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.43056em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span></span></span></span></span>:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><strong>Left-tailed test:</strong>  the area under the density curve from the critical value to the left is equal to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>α</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.43056em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span></span></span></span></span>;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Right-tailed test:</strong> the area under the density curve from the critical value to the right is equal to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>α</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.43056em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span></span></span></span></span>; and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Two-tailed test:</strong>  the area under the density curve from the left critical value to the left is equal to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>α</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mn>2</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha/2</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span><span class="mord">/2</span></span></span></span></span>, and the area under the curve from the right critical value to the right is equal to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>α</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mn>2</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha/2</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span><span class="mord">/2</span></span></span></span></span> as well; thus, total area equals  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>α</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.43056em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span></span></span></span></span>.</p>
</li>
</ul></div><figure class="imageBlock__image-align--center" style="width: 85%;"><picture><source media="only screen and (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 2) and (max-width: 800px)" type="image/webp" srcset="https://uploads-cdn.omnicalculator.com/images/crit_vals2.png?width=748&amp;enlarge=0&amp;format=webp"><source media="(max-width: 800px)" type="image/webp" srcset="https://uploads-cdn.omnicalculator.com/images/crit_vals2.png?width=374&amp;enlarge=0&amp;format=webp"><source media="only screen and (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 2)" type="image/webp" srcset="https://uploads-cdn.omnicalculator.com/images/crit_vals2.png?width=850&amp;enlarge=0&amp;format=webp"><source type="image/webp" srcset="https://uploads-cdn.omnicalculator.com/images/crit_vals2.png?width=425&amp;enlarge=0&amp;format=webp"><img src="https://uploads-cdn.omnicalculator.com/images/crit_vals2.png?width=425&amp;enlarge=0&amp;format=jpeg" alt="Critical values for symmetric distribution" class="imageBlock" loading="lazy" width="100%"></picture><figcaption>Critical values for symmetric distribution</figcaption></figure><div class="textBlock"><p>As you can see, finding the critical values for a two-tailed test with significance <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>α</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.43056em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span></span></span></span></span> boils down to finding both one-tailed critical values with a significance level of <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>α</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mn>2</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha/2</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span><span class="mord">/2</span></span></span></span></span>.</p></div></div></div></section><section data-testid="articleSection-3" data-cwv-id="calculator-article-section" id="critical-value-formulas" class="css-qtz96j e1p70fvu0"><h2 data-testid="articleSectionHeader-3" class="css-1xbj7gb">Critical value formulas</h2><div data-testid="articleSectionText" class="css-h9evcv e1p70fvu1"><div class="e1yds0yu0 css-12nedol e1m4c3o81"><div class="textBlock"><p>The formulae for the critical values involve the <strong>quantile function</strong>, <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>Q</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Q</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8777699999999999em;vertical-align:-0.19444em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span></span></span></span></span>, which is the inverse of the cumulative distribution function (<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">f</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{cdf}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.69444em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right:0.07778em;">cdf</span></span></span></span></span></span>) for the test statistic distribution (calculated under the assumption that H<sub>0</sub> holds!): <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>Q</mi><mo>=</mo><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">f</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Q = \mathrm{cdf}^{-1}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8777699999999999em;vertical-align:-0.19444em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2777777777777778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2777777777777778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8984479999999999em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right:0.07778em;">cdf</span></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.8984479999999999em;"><span style="top:-3.14734em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">−</span><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>.</p>
<p>Once we have agreed upon the value of <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>α</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.43056em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span></span></span></span></span>, the critical value formulae are the following:</p>
<ol>
<li><strong>Left-tailed  test</strong>:</li>
</ol></div><div class="mathBlock"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mspace width="2em"></mspace><mstyle mathsize="0.8em"><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mo>−</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">∞</mi><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>Q</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>α</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo stretchy="false">]</mo></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\qquad \footnotesize(-\infty, Q(\alpha)]</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8em;vertical-align:-0.2em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:2em;"></span><span class="mopen sizing reset-size6 size4">(</span><span class="mord sizing reset-size6 size4">−</span><span class="mord sizing reset-size6 size4">∞</span><span class="mpunct sizing reset-size6 size4">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.16666666666666666em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal sizing reset-size6 size4">Q</span><span class="mopen sizing reset-size6 size4">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal sizing reset-size6 size4" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span><span class="mclose sizing reset-size6 size4">)]</span></span></span></span></span></div><div class="textBlock"><ol start="2">
<li><strong>Right-tailed  test</strong>:</li>
</ol></div><div class="mathBlock"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mspace width="2em"></mspace><mstyle mathsize="0.8em"><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mi>Q</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>α</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">∞</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\qquad \footnotesize[Q(1-\alpha), \infty)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8em;vertical-align:-0.2em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:2em;"></span><span class="mopen sizing reset-size6 size4">[</span><span class="mord mathnormal sizing reset-size6 size4">Q</span><span class="mopen sizing reset-size6 size4">(</span><span class="mord sizing reset-size6 size4">1</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span><span class="mbin sizing reset-size6 size4">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.8em;vertical-align:-0.2em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal sizing reset-size6 size4" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span><span class="mclose sizing reset-size6 size4">)</span><span class="mpunct sizing reset-size6 size4">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.16666666666666666em;"></span><span class="mord sizing reset-size6 size4">∞</span><span class="mclose sizing reset-size6 size4">)</span></span></span></span></span></div><div class="textBlock"><ol start="3">
<li><strong>Two-tailed test</strong>:</li>
</ol></div><div class="mathBlock"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mspace width="2em"></mspace><mstyle mathsize="0.8em"><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mo>−</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">∞</mi><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>Q</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mfrac><mi>α</mi><mn>2</mn></mfrac><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo stretchy="false">]</mo><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mo>∪</mo><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mo stretchy="false">[</mo><mi>Q</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mfrac><mi>α</mi><mn>2</mn></mfrac><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">∞</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\qquad \footnotesize(-\infty, Q(\frac{\alpha}{2})] \ \cup \ [Q(1 - \frac{\alpha}{2}), \infty)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.5316480000000001em;vertical-align:-0.6016em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:2em;"></span><span class="mopen sizing reset-size6 size4">(</span><span class="mord sizing reset-size6 size4">−</span><span class="mord sizing reset-size6 size4">∞</span><span class="mpunct sizing reset-size6 size4">,</span><span class="mspace" reset-size6 size4"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter sizing reset-size4 size6"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:1.16256em;"><span style="top:-2.248em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">2</span></span></span><span style="top:-3.2255000000000003em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width:0.049em;"></span></span><span style="top:-3.732em;"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.752em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter sizing reset-size4 size6"></span></span><span class="mclose sizing reset-size6 size4">)]</span><span class="mspace sizing reset-size6 size4">&nbsp;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span><span class="mbin sizing class="strut" style="height:0.8em;vertical-align:-0.2em;"></span><span class="mopen sizing reset-size6 size4">[</span><span class="mord mathnormal sizing reset-size6 size4">Q</span><span class="mopen size4">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.5316480000000001em;vertical-align:-0.6016em;"></span><span class="mord sizing reset-size6 size4"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter sizing reset-size4 size6"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:1.16256em;"><span style="top:-2.248em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">2</span></span></span><span style="top:-3.2255000000000003em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width:0.049em;"></span></span><span style="top:-3.732em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.752em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter sizing reset-size4 size6"></span></span><span class="mclose sizing reset-size6 size4">)</span><span class="mpunct sizing reset-size6 size4">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.16666666666666666em;"></span><span class="mord sizing reset-size6 size4">∞</span><span class="mclose sizing reset-size6 size4">)</span></span></span></span></span></div><div class="textBlock"><p>In the case of a <strong>distribution symmetric about 0</strong>, the critical values for the two-tailed test are symmetric as well:</p></div><div class="mathBlock"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mrow><mstyle mathsize="0.9em"><mi>Q</mi><mrow><mo fence="true">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mfrac><mi>α</mi><mn>2</mn></mfrac><mo fence="true">)</mo></mrow><mo>=</mo><mo>−</mo><mi>Q</mi><mrow><mo fence="true">(</mo><mfrac><mi>α</mi><mn>2</mn></mfrac><mo fence="true">)</mo></mrow></mstyle></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\small Q\left(1 - \frac{\alpha}{2}\right) = -Q\left(\frac{\alpha}{2}\right)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.80002em;vertical-align:-0.6725200000000001em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal sizing reset-size6 size5">Q</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.16666666666666666em;"></span><span class="minner sizing reset-size6 size5"><span class="mopen sizing reset-size5 size6 delimcenter" style="top:0.024999999999999994em;"><span class="delimsizing size2">(</span></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter sizing reset-size5 size6"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:1.10756em;"><span style="top:-2.314em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">2</span></span></span><span style="top:-3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width:0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top:-3.677em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.686em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter sizing reset-size5 size6"></span></span><span class="mclose sizing reset-size5 size6 delimcenter" style="top:0.024999999999999994em;"><span class="delimsizing size2">)</span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2777777777777778em;"></span><span class="mrel sizing reset-size6 size5">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2777777777777778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.80002em;vertical-align:-0.6725200000000001em;"></span><span class="mord sizing reset-size6 size5">−</span><span class="mord mathnormal sizing reset-size6 size5">Q</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.16666666666666666em;"></span><span class="minner sizing reset-size6 size5"><span class="mopen sizing reset-size5 size6 delimcenter" style="top:0.024999999999999994em;"><span class="delimsizing size2">(</span></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter sizing reset-size5 size6"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:1.10756em;"><span style="top:-2.314em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">2</span></span></span><span style="top:-3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width:0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top:-3.677em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.686em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter sizing reset-size5 size6"></span></span><span class="mclose sizing reset-size5 size6 delimcenter" style="top:0.024999999999999994em;"><span class="delimsizing size2">)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></div></div></div></section><section data-testid="articleSection-4" data-cwv-id="calculator-article-section" id="how-to-calculate-critical-values" class="css-qtz96j e1p70fvu0"><h2 data-testid="articleSectionHeader-4" class="css-1xbj7gb">How to calculate critical values?</h2><div data-testid="articleSectionText" class="css-h9evcv e1p70fvu1"><div class="e1yds0yu0 css-12nedol e1m4c3o81"><div class="textBlock"><p>As we explained above, to compute critical values, you need to know the <strong>quantile function <code>Q</code></strong>  of a given probability distribution. For some distributions we can compute it by hand, however, the probability distributions that are the most widespread in hypothesis testing feature quite complicated formulae for  <code>Q</code>.</p>
<p>To find, e.g, z critical values or t critical values, you will need to use specialized <strong>statistical tables</strong>, which contain hundreds and hundreds of rows of data. This was the only available solution before the age of modern computers! Now, obviously, the best option is to use our critical value calculator! 😁</p></div></div></div></section><section data-testid="articleSection-5" data-cwv-id="calculator-article-section" id="z-critical-values" class="css-qtz96j e1p70fvu0"><h2 data-testid="articleSectionHeader-5" class="css-1xbj7gb">Z critical values</h2><div data-testid="articleSectionText" class="css-h9evcv e1p70fvu1"><div class="e1yds0yu0 css-12nedol e1m4c3o81"><div class="textBlock"><p>Use the <code>Z (standard normal)</code> option if your test statistic follows (at least approximately) the <strong>standard normal distribution N(0,1)</strong>.</p></div><figure class="imageBlock__image-align--center" style="width: 85%;"><img src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/03/Gauss_dichtefunktion.svg" alt="N(0,1) distribution density" class="imageBlock" loading="lazy" width="100%"><figcaption>StefanPohl / CC0 <span class="js-external-link-button link-like" data-href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Gauss_dichtefunktion.svg" role="button" tabindex="0">wikimedia.org</span></figcaption></figure><div class="textBlock"><p>In the formulae below, <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>u</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">u</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.43056em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">u</span></span></span></span></span> denotes the quantile function of the standard normal distribution N(0,1):</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Left-tailed Z critical value: <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>u</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>α</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">u(\alpha)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">u</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right-tailed Z critical value: <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>u</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>α</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">u(1-\alpha)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">u</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Two-tailed Z critical value: <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>±</mo><mi>u</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>α</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mn>2</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\pm u(1- \alpha/2)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">±</span><span class="mord mathnormal">u</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span><span class="mord">/2</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span></p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Check out <a href="/statistics/z-test" class="js-link">Z-test calculator</a> to learn more about the most common Z-test used on the population mean. There are also Z-tests for the difference between two population means, in particular, one between two proportions.</p></div></div></div></section><section data-testid="articleSection-6" data-cwv-id="calculator-article-section" id="t-critical-values" class="css-qtz96j e1p70fvu0"><h2 data-testid="articleSectionHeader-6" class="css-1xbj7gb">t critical values</h2><div data-testid="articleSectionText" class="css-h9evcv e1p70fvu1"><div class="e1yds0yu0 css-12nedol e1m4c3o81"><div class="textBlock"><p>Use the <code>t-Student</code> option if your test statistic follows the <strong>t-Student distribution</strong>. This distribution is <strong>similar to N(0,1)</strong>, but  <strong>its tails are fatter</strong> – the exact shape depends on the number of <em>degrees of freedom</em>. If this number is large (&gt;30), which generically happens for large samples, then the t-Student distribution is practically indistinguishable from N(0,1). Check our <a href="/statistics/t-statistic" class="js-link">t-statistic calculator</a> to compute the related test statistic.</p></div><figure class="imageBlock__image-align--center" style="width: 85%;"><picture><source media="only screen and (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 2) and (max-width: 800px)" type="image/webp" srcset="https://uploads-cdn.omnicalculator.com/images/Student_t_pdf.png?width=748&amp;enlarge=0&amp;format=webp"><source media="(max-width: 800px)" type="image/webp" srcset="https://uploads-cdn.omnicalculator.com/images/Student_t_pdf.png?width=374&amp;enlarge=0&amp;format=webp"><source media="only screen and (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 2)" type="image/webp" srcset="https://uploads-cdn.omnicalculator.com/images/Student_t_pdf.png?width=850&amp;enlarge=0&amp;format=webp"><source type="image/webp" srcset="https://uploads-cdn.omnicalculator.com/images/Student_t_pdf.png?width=425&amp;enlarge=0&amp;format=webp"><img src="https://uploads-cdn.omnicalculator.com/images/Student_t_pdf.png?width=425&amp;enlarge=0&amp;format=jpeg" alt="t-Student distribution densities" class="imageBlock" loading="lazy" width="100%"></picture><figcaption>Density of the t-distribution with ν degrees of freedom. <span class="js-external-link-button link-like" data-href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/3.0" tabindex="0">wikimedia.org</span></figcaption></figure><div class="textBlock"><p>In the formulae below,  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>Q</mi><mrow><mtext>t</mtext><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>d</mi></mrow></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Q_{\text{t}, d}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" class="vlist" style="height:0.3361079999999999em;"><span style="top:-2.5500000000000003em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">t</span></span><span class="mpunct mtight">,</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">d</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.286108em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> is the quantile function of the t-Student distribution with <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>d</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">d</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.69444em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">d</span></span></span></span></span> degrees of freedom:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Left-tailed t critical value: <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>Q</mi><mrow><mtext>t</mtext><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>d</mi></mrow></msub><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>α</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Q_{\text{t}, d}(\alpha)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.036108em;vertical-align:-0.286108em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3361079999999999em;"><span style="top:-2.5500000000000003em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">t</span></span><span class="mpunct mtight">,</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">d</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.286108em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right-tailed t critical value: <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>Q</mi><mrow><mtext>t</mtext><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>d</mi></mrow></msub><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>α</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Q_{\text{t}, d}(1 - \alpha)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.036108em;vertical-align:-0.286108em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3361079999999999em;"><span style="top:-2.5500000000000003em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">t</span></span><span class="mpunct mtight">,</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">d</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.286108em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Two-tailed t critical values: <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>±</mo><msub><mi>Q</mi><mrow><mtext>t</mtext><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>d</mi></mrow></msub><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>α</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mn>2</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\pm Q_{\text{t}, d}(1 - \alpha/2)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.036108em;vertical-align:-0.286108em;"></span><span class="mord">±</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3361079999999999em;"><span style="top:-2.5500000000000003em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">t</span></span><span class="mpunct mtight">,</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">d</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.286108em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span><span class="mord">/2</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span></p>
</li>
</ol></div><div class="textBlock"><p>Visit the <a href="/statistics/t-test" class="js-link">t-test calculator</a> to learn more about various t-tests: the one for a <strong>population mean with an unknown population standard deviation</strong>, those for the <strong>difference between the means of two populations</strong> (with either equal or unequal population standard deviations), as well as about the <strong>t-test for paired samples</strong>.</p></div></div></div></section><section data-testid="articleSection-7" data-cwv-id="calculator-article-section" id="how-do-i-find-t-critical-value-for-a-given-sample-size" class="css-qtz96j e1p70fvu0"><h2 data-testid="articleSectionHeader-7" class="css-1xbj7gb">How do I find t critical value for a given sample size?</h2><div data-testid="articleSectionText" class="css-h9evcv e1p70fvu1"><div class="e1yds0yu0 css-12nedol e1m4c3o81"><div class="textBlock"><p>To find a t critical value for the confidence level <code>α = 0.05</code>:</p>
<ol>
<li>Check if you perform a <strong>one- or two-tailed test</strong>.</li>
<li>Compute the degrees of freedom by subtracting 1 from the sample size:<br>
<code>Degree of Freedom = N – 1</code></li>
<li>For a one-tailed t-test:
<ul>
<li><strong>Left</strong>-tailed: critical value is the <strong><code>0.05</code>-th</strong> quantile of the t distribution with <code>N – 1</code> degrees of freedom.</li>
<li><strong>Right</strong>-tailed: critical value is the <strong><code>0.05</code>-th</strong> quantile of the t distribution with <code>N – 1</code> degrees of freedom.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Two-tailed test: critical value equals <strong><code>±(1-α/2)</code>-th</strong> quantile of the t distribution with <code>N – 1</code> degrees of freedom.</li>
<li>Open quantile <a href="/t-table" class="js-link">tables for t-distribution</a>. Look for the row corresponding to <code>N – 1</code> degrees of freedom and for the column corresponding to the significance level <code>0.05</code>. Copy the value that sits at the intersection of this row and column.</li>
<li>No <strong>quantile tables</strong>? Use an online critical value calculator!</li>
</ol></div></div></div></section><section data-testid="articleSection-8" data-cwv-id="calculator-article-section" id="t-critical-value-calculation-example" class="css-qtz96j e1p70fvu0"><h2 data-testid="articleSectionHeader-8" class="css-1xbj7gb">t critical value calculation: Example</h2><div data-testid="articleSectionText" class="css-h9evcv e1p70fvu1"><div class="e1yds0yu0 css-12nedol e1m4c3o81"><div class="textBlock"><p>Let us find the t critical value if the size of the sample is 5 and the significance level is 0.05.</p>
<p><strong>Solution:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Subtract 1 from the sample size to get the degree of freedom:<br>
<code>Degree of Freedom = N – 1 = 5-1 = 4</code></li>
<li>Now take a one-tailed or two-tailed t-distribution table. Search the value of the degree of freedom in the leftmost column of the table.</li>
<li>Now choose the value of the significance level in the topmost row of the t table.</li>
<li>To calculate the t critical value, get the value where both degrees of freedom and significance level intersect. In this case, the t critical value is <strong>2.132</strong>.</li>
</ol></div></div></div></section><section data-testid="articleSection-9" data-cwv-id="calculator-article-section" id="chi-square-critical-values-x" class="css-qtz96j e1p70fvu0"><h2 data-testid="articleSectionHeader-9" class="css-1xbj7gb">chi-square critical values (χ²)</h2><div data-testid="articleSectionText" class="css-h9evcv e1p70fvu1"><div class="e1yds0yu0 css-12nedol e1m4c3o81"><div class="textBlock"><p>Use the <code>χ² (chi-square)</code> option when performing a test in which the test statistic follows the <strong>χ²-distribution</strong>.</p>
<p>You need to determine the number of degrees of freedom of the χ²-distribution of your test statistic – below, we list them for the most commonly used χ²-tests.</p></div><figure class="imageBlock__image-align--center" style="width: 85%;"><img src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/35/Chi-square_pdf.svg" alt="Chi-square distribution densities" class="imageBlock" loading="lazy" width="100%"><figcaption>Density of the χ²-distribution with k degrees of freedom. <span class="js-external-link-button link-like" data-href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/3.0" role="button" tabindex="0">Geek3 / CC BY</span> <span class="js-external-link-button link-like" data-href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Chi-square_pdf.svg" role="button" tabindex="0">wikimedia.org</span></figcaption></figure><div class="textBlock"><p>Here we give the formulae for chi square critical values;  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math encoding="application/x-tex">Q_{\chi^2,   d}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" class="vlist" style="height:0.3448em;"><span style="top:-2.52238em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">χ</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mpunct mtight">,</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">d</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" <ol>
<li>
<p>Left-tailed χ² critical value: <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>Q</mi><mrow><msup><mi>χ</mi><mn>2</mn></msup><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>d</mi></mrow></msub><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>α</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Q_{\chi^2, d}(\alpha)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.063728em;vertical-align:-0.313728em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3448em;"><span style="top:-2.52238em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">χ</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.7463142857142857em;"><span style="top:-2.786em;margin-right:0.07142857142857144em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.5em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size3 size1 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mpunct mtight">,</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">d</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.313728em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right-tailed χ² critical value: <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>Q</mi><mrow><msup><mi>χ</mi><mn>2</mn></msup><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>d</mi></mrow></msub><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>−</mo><mi>α</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Q_{\chi^2, d}(1 - \alpha)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.063728em;vertical-align:-0.313728em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3448em;"><span style="top:-2.52238em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">χ</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.7463142857142857em;"><span style="top:-2.786em;margin-right:0.07142857142857144em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.5em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size3 size1 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mpunct mtight">,</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">d</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.313728em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Two-tailed χ² critical values: <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>Q</mi><mrow><msup><mi>χ</mi><mn>2</mn></msup><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>d</mi></mrow></msub><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>α</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mn>2</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Q_{\chi^2, d}(\alpha/2)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.063728em;vertical-align:-0.313728em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3448em;"><span style="top:-2.52238em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">χ</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.7463142857142857em;"><span style="top:-2.786em;margin-right:0.07142857142857144em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.5em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size3 size1 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mpunct mtight">,</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">d</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.313728em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span><span class="mord">/2</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span> and <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>Q</mi><mrow><msup><mi>χ</mi><mn>2</mn></msup><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>d</mi></mrow></msub><mo \alpha/2)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.063728em;vertical-align:-0.313728em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">Q</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.3448em;"><span style="top:-2.52238em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">χ</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.7463142857142857em;"><span style="top:-2.786em;margin-right:0.07142857142857144em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.5em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size3 size1 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mpunct mtight">,</span><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">d</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.313728em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.0037em;">α</span><span class="mord">/2</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span></p>
</li>
</ol></div><div class="textBlock"><p>Several different tests lead to a χ²-score:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><strong>Goodness-of-fit test</strong>: does the empirical distribution agree with the expected distribution?</p>
<p>This test is <strong>right-tailed</strong>. Its test statistic follows the χ²-distribution with <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k - 1</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.77777em;vertical-align:-0.08333em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.03148em;">k</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.64444em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span></span></span></span></span> degrees of freedom, where <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>k</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">k</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.69444em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.03148em;">k</span></span></span></span></span> is the number of classes into which the sample is divided.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Independence test</strong>: is there a statistically significant relationship between two variables?</p>
<p>This test is also  <strong>right-tailed</strong>, and its test statistic is computed from the contingency table. There are  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>r</mi><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>c</mi><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(r - 1)(c - 1)</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.02778em;">r</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mclose">)</span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord mathnormal">c</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1em;vertical-align:-0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span> degrees of freedom, where <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>r</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">r</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.43056em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.02778em;">r</span></span></span></span></span> is the number of rows, and <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>c</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">c</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.43056em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">c</span></span></span></span></span> is the number of columns in the contingency table.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Test for the variance of normally distributed data</strong>: does this variance have some pre-determined value?</p>
<p>This test can be <strong>one- or two-tailed!</strong> Its test statistic has the χ²-distribution with <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>n</mi><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">n - 1</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.66666em;vertical-align:-0.08333em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">n</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right:0.2222222222222222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.64444em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span></span></span></span></span> degrees of freedom, where <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>n</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">n</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.43056em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">n</span></span></span></span></span> is the sample size.</p>
</li>
</ul></div></div></div></section><section data-testid="articleSection-10" data-cwv-id="calculator-article-section" id="f-critical-values" class="css-qtz96j e1p70fvu0"><h2 data-testid="articleSectionHeader-10" class="css-1xbj7gb">F critical values</h2><div data-testid="articleSectionText" class="css-h9evcv e1p70fvu1"><div class="e1yds0yu0 css-12nedol e1m4c3o81"><div class="textBlock"><p>Finally, choose  <code>F (Fisher-Snedecor)</code>  if your test statistic follows the <strong>F-distribution</strong>. This distribution has a <strong>pair of degrees of freedom</strong>.</p>
<p>Let us see how those degrees of freedom arise. Assume that you have two independent random variables, <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>X</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">X</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.68333em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.07847em;">X</span></span></span></span></span> and <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>Y</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">Y</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.68333em;vertical-align:0em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right:0.22222em;">Y</span></span></span></span></span>, that follow χ²-distributions with   <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>d</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">d_1</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.84444em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">d</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.30110799999999993em;"><span style="top:-2.5500000000000003em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> and <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>d</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">d_2</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:0.84444em;vertical-align:-0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal">d</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.30110799999999993em;"><span style="top:-2.5500000000000003em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> degrees of freedom, respectively. If you now consider the  ratio <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mfrac><mi>X</mi><msub><mi>d</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mfrac><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>:</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mfrac><mi>Y</mi><msub><mi>d</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mfrac><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(\frac{X}{d_1}):(\frac{Y}{d_2})</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height:1.317431em;vertical-align:-0.44509999999999994em;"></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.872331em;"><span style="top:-2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight">d</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.31731428571428577em;"><span style="top:-2.357em;margin-left:0em;margin-right:0.07142857142857144em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:2.5em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size3 size1 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height:0.143em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="top:-3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width:0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top:-3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height:3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mathnormal mtight" style="margin-right:0.07847em;">X</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist"
